## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator, typically modeled as a second-order ODE rewritten as a first-order system with state (x, v) and possible explicit time forcing t. Common structures combine a restoring force depending on x, damping depending on v, and optional periodic/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Conservative oscillator (potential-gradient form): dv_dt = -dU_dx(x) (motion in 1D potential; no dissipation/forcing)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations about equilibrium; Hooke-like restoring)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator; dissipation proportional to velocity)
- Constant (bias) acceleration / shifted equilibrium: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium offset; constant external load)
- Pendulum small-angle with damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (pendulum linearization; same structure as damped SHO)
- Pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (finite-angle pendulum with damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear springs/potentials)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in oscillatory motion)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip tendency; velocity-direction-dependent friction)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillator with amplitude regulation)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation via nonlinear damping in v)
- Forced Duffing / driven oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; parametric resonance)
- General polynomial state-force model: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - (c3 * v + c4 * v**3) + c5 * cos(c6 * t) (common symbolic-regression template for nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring forces are typically odd in x around a symmetric equilibrium: dv_dt often contains -x, -x**3, -sin(c*x), implying acceleration points back toward x=0.
- Damping is typically odd in v: terms like -v, -v*Abs(v), -(v**3) dissipate energy and reduce oscillation amplitude.
- If the system is conservative (no damping/forcing), dv_dt depends on x but not on v or t; adding v-terms breaks energy conservation.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is indicated by the sign of the x**3 term: -c*x**3 with c>0 increases effective stiffness with amplitude; c<0 decreases it.
- Self-excited oscillations (limit cycles) often appear as state-dependent damping such as (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v, which injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- External driving typically enters as additive periodic functions of t (e.g., cos(c*t), sin(c*t)); resonance appears when the driving frequency matches the natural frequency scale set by the x-term.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when t-modulation multiplies x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) rather than being purely additive forcing.
- Non-smooth frictional effects are indicated by sign(v) or piecewise-like dependence on v, often producing corners in phase portraits and amplitude-dependent decay.

Structure desc      : The formula is an additive combination of (i) a linear term in x, (ii) a linear term in v, (iii) a sinusoid in x of the form c2*sin(c3+c4*x), and (iv) a time-only oscillation c5*exp(c6*t)*cos(c7*t) where the cosine is modulated by a slow exponential envelope. Variable roles: x appears both linearly and inside the sine argument (frequency set by c4=1.397), v appears only as a small linear correction (c1=-0.0517 vs c0=-0.7546 and |c2|=1.34), and t appears only in the modulated cosine (rate c6=0.0321, angular frequency c7=0.938). With c6 close to 0 the envelope varies slowly, so the time term behaves approximately like a modest-amplitude cosine (~0.136*cos(0.938*t)), making the dominant behavior a negative linear trend in x plus a larger-amplitude x-sinusoid with small v and weak, slowly growing oscillatory t-variation.
Fitted params       : c0=-7.5459e-01, c1=-5.1746e-02, c2=-1.3415e+00, c3=2.0617e-01, c4=1.3974e+00, c5=1.3563e-01, c6=3.2125e-02, c7=9.3811e-01

GT (fully concrete) is
\[
F(x,t,v)=0.415528810853583\sin t\;-\;0.0493727442837992\,v^3\;-\;0.291667748408705\,|v|^{1/3}\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x(0.0222734330694684\,t+1)\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x.
\]
So GT contains **all** of these structural features simultaneously:

1) a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no \(x\) inside the sine),  
2) a **cubic** damping term \(v^3\) (odd polynomial),  
3) a **fractional absolute-power** term \(|v|^{1/3}\) (non-polynomial, even in \(v\)),  
4) an \(x\,t\) cross term: \(-K\,x\,t\) (linear in both),  
5) an additional linear-in-\(x\) term (actually two linear-in-\(x\) contributions combine to \(-2.0586\,x\)).

Any candidate that cannot simultaneously represent items (1)–(4) (and the correct linear \(x\) part) cannot be made identical for all real \(x,t,v\).
